1. # Post-Mortem Report: Agentic Development of Epic #2
2. 
3. ## Instructions
4. 
5. Generate a comprehensive post-mortem report for the agentic development work on Epic https://github.com/edburns/Build26-BRK206-your-agent-anywhere-multiclient-multidevice-with-github-copilot-sdk/issues/2.
6. 
7. The report should be written to `dd-3017826-java-real-estate-demo-remove-before-merge/dd-3029269-post-mortem-report.md`.
8. 
9. ---
10. 
11. ## Data Sources
12. 
13. ### 1. GitHub Issues and PRs
14. 
15. Fetch all sub-issues of https://github.com/edburns/Build26-BRK206-your-agent-anywhere-multiclient-multidevice-with-github-copilot-sdk/issues/2 using `gh` CLI. **Exclude** any issue whose title starts with `[ABORTED]`.
16. 
17. For each non-aborted sub-issue, collect via `gh` CLI:
18. - Issue number, title, and body
19. - The linked PR (from issue timeline or cross-references)
20. - PR number, title, headRefName, baseRefName
21. - PR commits: `gh api /repos/OWNER/REPO/pulls/$PR/commits --paginate`
22. - PR reviews: `gh api /repos/OWNER/REPO/pulls/$PR/reviews`
23. - PR review comments: `gh api /repos/OWNER/REPO/pulls/$PR/comments --paginate`
24. - PR merge status and merge commit
25. - PR diff stats: `gh pr view $PR --json additions,deletions,changedFiles`
26. 
27. The repo is `edburns/Build26-BRK206-your-agent-anywhere-multiclient-multidevice-with-github-copilot-sdk`.
28. 
29. ### 2. Shepherd Task Logs
30. 
31. Read the JSONL logs from these directories (relative to repo root):
32. 
33. ```
34. shepherd-tasks-20260708-1203
35. shepherd-tasks-20260708-1233
36. shepherd-tasks-20260708-1244
37. shepherd-tasks-20260708-1340
38. shepherd-tasks-20260708-1918
39. ```
40. 
41. Each directory contains files like `phase1-task-TIMESTAMP-ISSUE.json`, `phase2-task-TIMESTAMP-ISSUE.json`, and `.md` status files. Parse the JSONL files to extract:
42. - Timestamps (first and last event per file)
43. - Tool call counts and success/failure rates
44. - `assistant.message` events with tool requests (to count tool calls per phase)
45. - `user.message` events (to see the prompts sent)
46. 
47. ---
48. 
49. ## Report Structure
50. 
51. ### Section 1: Executive Summary
52. 
53. Brief overview: how many tasks, how many succeeded, total wall-clock time, total AI credits.
54. 
55. ### Section 2: System Architecture
56. 
57. Describe the three-agent system:
58. 
59. 1. **Copilot Coding Agent (CCA)**: Does the initial implementation upon assignment of an issue. Runs on GitHub's infrastructure.
60. 2. **Copilot Code Review Agent (CCRA)**: Reviews the initial implementation when the PR is marked **Ready for review**. Runs on GitHub's infrastructure.
61. 3. **Local Copilot CLI**: Fetches, assesses, and maybe applies each comment in a CCRA batch, making a single commit for each comment with a single push to the base branch and re-requesting review. It repeats this process until there are no more comments or 8 comment iterations have been reached, whichever comes first. Runs locally via `copilot --yolo`.
62. 
63. ### Section 3: Per-Task Metrics
64. 
65. For each non-aborted sub-issue, create a row/subsection with:
66. 
67. #### Throughput & Convergence (original proposed metrics)
68. - Number of commits comprising the initial CCA implementation
69. - Number of CCRA rounds performed by the local copilot
70. - Number of commits per CCRA round
71. - Quality of the CCRA commits — did they "converge" (i.e., did successive rounds produce fewer comments)?
72. - Whether the max CCRA rounds (8) was hit
73. 
74. #### CCA Effectiveness (was the initial work good?)
75. - Lines changed by CCRA fixes vs. total lines in initial implementation (rework ratio)
76. - Did the implementation satisfy the issue requirements? (assess from issue body vs. PR diff)
77. - Did CCA follow stated constraints (e.g., Jakarta Data not raw JPA, `@CopilotTool` annotation, EE11 standards)?
78. 
79. #### CCRA Signal Quality (was the review useful?)
80. - Comments dismissed as no-merit vs. accepted — false-positive rate
81. - Severity distribution (High/Medium/Low from the review body)
82. - Category breakdown (correctness bug, style nit, security, missing feature)
83. - Did round N+1 introduce new comments on code that round N touched? (oscillation/regression detection)
84. 
85. #### Local Copilot Accuracy (did it apply fixes well?)
86. - Fixes that broke compilation or tests (look for failed tool calls in JSONL)
87. - Comments where local copilot disagreed with the suggested remedy and devised its own
88. 
89. #### System-Level Health
90. - Did the task require manual intervention?
91. - Wall-clock time from issue assignment to merge
92. - Tasks that failed outright (no PR, merge conflict, skill error)
93. 
94. ### Section 4: Aggregate Statistics
95. 
96. Across all tasks:
97. - Total commits by CCA
98. - Total CCRA review rounds
99. - Total CCRA comments generated
100. - Total CCRA comments accepted vs. dismissed
101. - Average CCRA rounds per task
102. - Tasks hitting the 8-round cap
103. - Tasks requiring manual intervention
104. 
105. ### Section 5: AI Credits
106. 
107. Report the total number of AI credits used across all three agent types:
108. - **CCA credits**: Check via `gh api /repos/OWNER/REPO/actions/runs` for Copilot coding agent runs, or from the GitHub billing/usage page if accessible.
109. - **CCRA credits**: Count the number of review rounds (each review request consumes credits).
110. - **Local Copilot CLI credits**: Parse the JSONL logs for token usage. Look for `outputTokens` and `inputTokens` fields in `assistant.message` events. Sum across all phase1 and phase2 logs in all shepherd-tasks directories.
111. 
112. Present a breakdown table and total.
113. 
114. ### Section 6: Wall-Clock Timeline
115. 
116. - **Start**: First event timestamp in `shepherd-tasks-20260708-1203/` (the earliest JSONL file)
117. - **End**: Last event timestamp in `shepherd-tasks-20260708-1918/` (the latest JSONL file)
118. - **Total elapsed**: End minus Start
119. - Include a timeline showing when each batch started and ended, and notable events (manual interventions, script restarts between batches)
120. 
121. ### Section 7: Observations and Recommendations
122. 
123. Based on the data collected, provide:
124. - What worked well
125. - What didn't work well
126. - Specific recommendations for improving each agent's contribution
127. - Recommendations for the shepherd orchestration scripts
128. - Any patterns noticed (e.g., certain types of issues converge faster, certain CCRA comment categories are always noise)
129. 
130. ---
131. 
132. ## Format
133. 
134. - Use Markdown tables for per-task metrics
135. - Use Markdown for the narrative sections
136. - Include raw numbers and percentages where applicable
137. - When citing specific commits, use short hashes
138. - When citing specific review comments, include the `discussion_r*` ID
139.
````

1. # Session Memory: Shepherd Tasks 20260718-1827
2. 
3. ## What We Did This Session
4. 
5. ### Context
6. Shepherded 6 Python agent demo task issues (#34–#39) through a multi-agent pipeline using `shepherd-task-given-list.ps1`. This was the **successful run** after diagnosing and fixing multiple failures from earlier attempts (20260717-1748, 20260717-1936, 20260717-2022).
7. 
8. ### Bugs Diagnosed & Fixed
9. 
10. 1. **Idle-kill timeout bug** — The Copilot CLI runtime terminates sessions ~60s after an `assistant.idle` event fires. This happened when Phase 2 agents backgrounded their polling commands (exceeding `initial_wait: 120s`). The agent would have no pending tool calls, go idle, and get killed before the Copilot code review arrived (~180s).
11.    - **Fix:** Added `⚠️ CRITICAL: Never go idle while waiting` directive to all 3 skills with 4 rules: use `initial_wait ≥ 600`, never background poll commands, always have a tool call pending, emit progress messages.
12. 
13. 2. **Missing Copilot code review request** — Marking a PR as "Ready for review" does NOT automatically trigger Copilot code review. The Phase 2 skill was waiting for a review that was never requested.
14.    - **Fix:** Added explicit `gh pr edit $PR_NUMBER --add-reviewer "copilot-pull-request-reviewer"` to Step 1 of `shepherd-task-from-ready-to-merged-to-base`.
15. 
16. 3. **PR base branch merge-to-wrong-target (issue #32)** — Phase 1 agent committed directly to `edburns/28-python-agent-demo` (the BASE_BRANCH) instead of creating a child branch. This made head==base when trying to retarget. Phase 2 then rationalized the error and merged to `main`.
17.    - **Root cause:** The CCA didn't create a feature branch off BASE_BRANCH.
18.    - **Script gap:** `shepherd-task.ps1` line 153 doesn't check exit code of `gh pr edit --base`. (Not yet fixed per user decision.)
19. 
20. 4. **OTEL file exporter not flushing (copilot-agent-runtime#13047)** — OTEL spans collected in memory but never flushed to disk when `copilot` is invoked via piped stdin. Works with `-p` flag. Bug filed.
21. 
22. ### Scripts & Skills Modified
23. 
24. | File | Change |
25. |------|--------|
26. | `skills/shepherd-task-from-ready-to-merged-to-base/SKILL.md` | Idle prevention, explicit review request, initial_wait callout |

28. | `skills/shepherd-task-approve-workflows-and-wait-for-completion/SKILL.md` | Idle prevention |
29. | `plugins/shepherd-task/scripts/shepherd-task.ps1` | OTEL absolute paths |
30. | `plugins/shepherd-task/scripts/shepherd-task.sh` | OTEL absolute paths |
31. | `plugins/shepherd-task/scripts/shepherd-task-given-list.ps1` | Log dir announcement |
32. | `plugins/shepherd-task/scripts/shepherd-task-given-list.sh` | Log dir announcement |

34. | `plugins/shepherd-task/scripts/shepherd-task-monitor.sh` | **NEW** — real-time monitoring |
35.

Follow the instructions in the skill context.","detailedContent":"Skill loaded successfully ✅\n\n# Skill: Shepherd Task from Ready for Review to Merged\n\n## Purpose\n\nAutomate the lifecycle of a task PR from marking as **Ready for review** through Copilot code review comment resolution and merge to the specified base branch. This is a follow-up skill intended to be run after `shepherd-task-from-assignment-to-ready`.\n\n## Inputs\n\n- `TASK_ISSUE`: The issue number (e.g., `1850`) or URL of the child task.\n- `BASE_BRANCH`: The base branch the task PR should target (e.g., `edburns/1810-java-tool-ergonomics-tool-as-lambda`).\n- `REPO`: Repository in `OWNER/REPO` format (default: `github/copilot-sdk`).\n- `REMOTE`: Git remote to push to (default: `upstream`).\n\n## Prerequisites\n\n- The `shepherd-task-from-assignment-to-ready` skill has completed successfully for this task.\n- `PR_NUMBER` is known (the PR created by Copilot for this task). For discussion: `jtbdtask-pr`.\n- `gh` CLI authenticated with sufficient permissions.\n- The PR is currently in draft state with all CI checks passing.\n\n---\n\n## ⚠️ CRITICAL: Never go idle while waiting\n\nThe `copilot --yolo` runtime **terminates the session shortly after the agent goes idle** (i.e., when there are no pending tool calls). If you launch a long-running polling command with a short `initial_wait` and then say \"I'll check back when it completes,\" the runtime will kill the session before the command finishes.\n\n**Rules for all polling and waiting steps:**\n\n1. ✅✅✅ **ALWAYS use `initial_wait` ≥ 600 seconds** (10 minutes) on any polling/waiting command. This keeps the agent blocked on the tool call rather than going idle. ✅✅✅\n2. ❌❌❌ **NEVER background a polling command and then end your turn with no tool calls.** If a command exceeds `initial_wait`, immediately issue another tool call (e.g., `read_powershell`) to stay active. ❌❌❌\n3. ❌❌❌ **NEVER say \"I'll check back when it completes\" or \"Waiting for notification.\"** These phrases mean you are going idle, which KILLS THE SESSION. ❌❌❌\n4. ✅✅✅ **ALWAYS prefer a single blocking poll** over launching a background command and waiting for a notification. ✅✅✅\n\n---\n\n## Procedure\n\n### Step 0: Find the PR\n\nUse the same multi-strategy approach as the assignment skill:\n\n1. **Issue timeline** — query `gh api \"/repos/$REPO/issues/$TASK_ISSUE/timeline\"` for cross-referenced open PRs.\n2. **PR body search** — search open PR bodies for `#$TASK_ISSUE`.\n3. **Title/branch match** — regex match on title or headRefName.\n\nIf none of these find the PR, fail the skill and report the error.\n\n### Step 1: Mark the PR as Ready for Review and request Copilot review\n\n```bash\ngh pr ready $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO\ngh pr edit $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --add-reviewer \"copilot-pull-request-reviewer\"\n```\n\n**Important:** Copilot code review is NOT automatically triggered when a PR is taken out of draft state. You must explicitly request it.\n\n### Step 2: Wait for Copilot code review agent to complete\n\nWait for the Copilot code review agent to post its findings.\n\nPoll the PR reviews and comments using **multiple detection strategies** (any match is sufficient).\n\n**⚠️ Use `initial_wait: 660` (11 minutes) on this polling command to prevent the session from going idle and being killed.**\n\n**Strategy A:** A review whose body matches `\"Copilot.s findings\"` (original format).\n\n**Strategy B:** A review whose body matches `\"Pull request overview\"` (alternate format).\n\n**Strategy C:** A review from a user whose login contains `\"copilot-pull-request-reviewer\"` (handles `[bot]` suffix).\n\n**Strategy D:** Line-level review comments from user `Copilot` on the PR.\n\n```bash\n# Poll every 30 seconds for up to 10 minutes\nTIMEOUT=600\nINTERVAL=30\nELAPSED=0\n\nwhile [ $ELAPSED -lt $TIMEOUT ]; do\n  # Strategy A: Original \"Copilot's findings\" header\n  FINDINGS=$(gh api \"/repos/$REPO/pulls/$PR_NUMBER/reviews\" \\\n    --jq '.[] | select(.body | test(\"Copilot.s findings\")) | {id: .id, body: .body}' 2>/dev/null | tail -1)\n\n  # Strategy B: Alternate \"Pull request overview\" header\n  if [ -z \"$FINDINGS\" ]; then\n    FINDINGS=$(gh api \"/repos/$REPO/pulls/$PR_NUMBER/reviews\" \\\n      --jq '.[] | select(.body | test(\"Pull request overview\")) | {id: .id, body: .body}' 2>/dev/null | tail -1)\n  fi\n\n  # Strategy C: Any review from the copilot-pull-request-reviewer bot\n  if [ -z \"$FINDINGS\" ]; then\n    FINDINGS=$(gh api \"/repos/$REPO/pulls/$PR_NUMBER/reviews\" \\\n      --jq '.[] | select(.user.login | test(\"copilot-pull-request-reviewer\")) | {id: .id, body: .body}' 2>/dev/null | tail -1)\n  fi\n\n  # Strategy D: Line-level comments from user \"Copilot\"\n  if [ -z \"$FINDINGS\" ]; then\n    FINDINGS=$(gh api \"/repos/$REPO/pulls/$PR_NUMBER/comments\" \\\n      --jq '.[] | select(.user.login == \"Copilot\") | {id: .id, body: .body}' 2>/dev/null | head -1)\n  fi\n\n  if [ -n \"$FINDINGS\" ]; then\n    break\n  fi\n\n  sleep $INTERVAL\n  ELAPSED=$((ELAPSED + INTERVAL))\ndone\n```\n\nSearch for similar text to identify the batch of review findings (`jtbdtask-pr-comments`).\n\nIf **Comments generated: 0** (or no comments for this round), skip to **Step 15**.\n\nWhen `jtbdtask-pr-comments` has been identified, proceed.\n\n### Step 3: Determine N (number of comments)\n\n❌❌❌ DO NOT TAKE ANY ACTION ON COMMENTS ALREADY MARKED **Resolved**. ❌❌❌\n\nExtract the number of comments from the **Comments generated:** line in the findings header. There will be exactly N individual review comments in this batch to address.\n\n### Step 4: Fetch upstream and set up local worktree\n\n❌❌❌ This part of the work does not use the remote agent. All comment resolution is done locally. ❌❌❌\n\n```bash\n# Fetch upstream to get the topic branch\ngit fetch upstream\n\n# Get the currently logged in username\nGH_CURRENT_USER=$(gh api /user --jq '.login')\n\n# Get the topic branch name for the PR\nJTBDTASK_BRANCH=$(gh pr view $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --json headRefName --jq '.headRefName')\n\n# Create a worktree for local review work — as a SIBLING of the current repo clone, not inside it.\ngit worktree add \"../review-copilot-pr-$PR_NUMBER\" \"upstream/$JTBDTASK_BRANCH\"\n```\n\nFor discussion, this worktree is the `jtbdtask-pr-comments-comment-worktree`.\n\n### Step 5: Approve workflows and wait for completion\n\nInvoke the **`shepherd-task-approve-workflows-and-wait-for-completion`** skill (`skills/shepherd-task-approve-workflows-and-wait-for-completion/SKILL.md`) with:\n\n- `REPO` = `$REPO`\n- `JTBDTASK_BRANCH` = the PR's topic branch\n- `PR_NUMBER` = `$PR_NUMBER`\n\nThis ensures any pending workflow runs triggered by prior pushes are approved and complete before gathering review comments.\n\n### Step 6: Gather all review comments\n\n```bash\n# Get all review comments from the Copilot code review batch.\n# The reviewer may appear as \"copilot-pull-request-reviewer[bot]\" or \"Copilot\" depending on the repo.\ngh api \"/repos/$REPO/pulls/$PR_NUMBER/comments\" \\\n  --jq '.[] | select(.user.login | test(\"copilot-pull-request-reviewer|Copilot\")) | {id: .id, path: .path, line: .line, body: .body, in_reply_to_id: .in_reply_to_id}'\n```\n\nIdentify each individual comment. Each has a unique `id` (e.g., `discussion_r3456155645`-style reference). For discussion, each is a `jtbdtask-pr-comments-comment`.\n\n### Step 7: Address each review comment locally\n\nFor each review comment (`jtbdtask-pr-comments-comment`), working in the `jtbdtask-pr-comments-comment-worktree`:\n\n#### 7.1: Evaluate the comment\n\n- Carefully consider the comment and judge its merit.\n- **If there is no merit:** mark the comment as resolved with an explanatory note (defer the resolution reply until Step 9).\n- **If there is merit:** evaluate the suggested remedy.\n  - If you agree with the suggested remedy, proceed with it.\n  - If you disagree with the suggested remedy, devise a better remedy and proceed with that.\n\n#### 7.2: Implement the fix\n\n- Implement the remedy in the `jtbdtask-pr-comments-comment-worktree`.\n- Use the appropriate language coding skill in `skills/` to know how to run tests.\n- If there are a large number of tests:\n   - ❌❌❌ DO NOT RUN THE FULL TEST SUITE at this stage. ❌❌❌ .\n   - ✅✅✅ Only run the tests directly related to the fix, in isolation. ✅✅✅ .\n- Otherwise, if there is not a large number of tests:\n   - Run all the tests.\n- **If the commit touches any Java code, YOU MUST ALWAYS RUN `mvn spotless:apply` in the java directory before each commit.**\n\n#### 7.3: Commit locally (do not push)\n\n- Once the relevant tests pass, commit the fix.\n- ❌❌❌ Do NOT push yet. ❌❌❌\n- Keep track of the commit hash — you will need it when replying to the review comment.\n\n### Step 8: Push all fixes to `$REMOTE`\n\nOnce **all** N review comments have been addressed locally:\n\n```bash\n# Push from the worktree to the configured remote (sibling directory)\ncd \"../review-copilot-pr-$PR_NUMBER\"\ngit push \"$REMOTE\" HEAD:$JTBDTASK_BRANCH\n```\n\n### Step 9: Reply to each review comment and resolve the thread\n\nFor each `jtbdtask-pr-comments-comment`:\n\n1. State what you did to address the comment. If the action corresponds to a commit, include the hash: \"Fixed in `<hash>`\".\n2. Reply to the comment.\n3. Resolve the review thread.\n\nTo reply to the comment:\n\n```bash\n# Reply to a specific review comment\ngh api --method POST \"/repos/$REPO/pulls/$PR_NUMBER/comments/$COMMENT_ID/replies\" \\\n  -f \"body=Fixed in $COMMIT_HASH. Get the GraphQL thread node ID for the comment\nTHREAD_ID=$(gh api graphql -F number=$PR_NUMBER -f query='\nquery($number: Int!) {\n  repository(owner: \"github\", name: \"copilot-sdk\") {\n    pullRequest(number: $number) {\n      reviewThreads(first: 100) {\n        nodes {\n          id\n          isResolved\n          comments(first: 1) { nodes { databaseId } }\n        }\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}' --jq \".data.repository.pullRequest.reviewThreads.nodes[] | select(.comments.nodes[0].databaseId == $COMMENT_ID) | .id\")\n\n# 2. Resolve the thread\ngh api graphql -f query=\"\nmutation {\n  resolveReviewThread(input: {threadId: \\\"$THREAD_ID\\\"}) {\n    thread { id isResolved }\n  }\n}\"\n```\n\n### Step 10: Wait for CI to run\n\nThe push triggers CI/CD. Follow the instructions in the skill context.","detailedContent":"Skill loaded successfully ✅\n\n# Skill: Shepherd Task to Ready for Review\n\n## Purpose\n\nAutomate the lifecycle of a child **Task** issue from \"assigned to Copilot\" through CI passing and review-agent feedback resolution, stopping just before marking the PR as **Ready for review**.\n\n## Inputs\n\n- `TASK_ISSUE`: The issue number (e.g., `1850`) or URL of the child task to shepherd.\n- `BASE_BRANCH`: The base branch the task PR should target (default: `upstream/edburns/1810-java-tool-ergonomics-tool-as-lambda`).\n- `REPO`: Repository in `OWNER/REPO` format (default: `github/copilot-sdk`).\n\n## Prerequisites\n\n- `gh` CLI authenticated with sufficient permissions (issues, PRs, actions, reviews).\n- The task issue already exists and has a clear description of work to do.\n- The base branch exists in the repository.\n\n---\n\n## Procedure\n\n### Step 1: Assign the task to @Copilot\n\nUse the GitHub Issues REST API with the `agent_assignment.base_branch` parameter. This is the **only 100% reliable method** — it passes `BASE_BRANCH` directly to CCA as a first-class input, so it cannot default to `main`.\n\n> [!NOTE]\n> Do **not** use `gh issue edit --add-assignee \"@copilot\"` here. That command uses the plain assignees endpoint which has no `base_branch` parameter; CCA will default to `main`.\n\n```bash\ngh api \\\n  --method POST \\\n  -H \"Accept: application/vnd.github+json\" \\\n  -H \"X-GitHub-Api-Version: 2022-11-28\" \\\n  /repos/$REPO/issues/$TASK_ISSUE/assignees \\\n  --input - <<< \"{\n    \\\"assignees\\\": [\\\"copilot-swe-agent[bot]\\\"],\n    \\\"agent_assignment\\\": {\n      \\\"target_repo\\\": \\\"$REPO\\\",\n      \\\"base_branch\\\": \\\"$BASE_BRANCH\\\"\n    }\n  }\"\n```\n\n> **PowerShell equivalent** (when running on Windows):\n> ```powershell\n> $body = @{\n>     assignees        = @(\"copilot-swe-agent[bot]\")\n>     agent_assignment = @{\n>         target_repo = $REPO\n>         base_branch = $BASE_BRANCH\n>     }\n> } | ConvertTo-Json -Depth 3\n> gh api `\n>   --method POST `\n>   -H \"Accept: application/vnd.github+json\" `\n>   -H \"X-GitHub-Api-Version: 2022-11-28\" `\n>   /repos/$REPO/issues/$TASK_ISSUE/assignees `\n>   --input - <<< $body\n> ```\n\nThis triggers Copilot to:\n1. Create a topic branch from `$BASE_BRANCH`.\n2. Open a draft PR targeting `$BASE_BRANCH`.\n3. Push initial commits.\n\n### Step 2: Find the corresponding PR\n\nUse **all three** of the following strategies (in order) each polling iteration. Copilot often creates PRs whose title or branch name does NOT contain the issue number — it may use a descriptive name instead. Therefore, relying on title/branch regex alone is insufficient.\n\n#### Strategy A: Query the issue timeline for linked PRs\n\nThe GitHub timeline API shows PRs linked via \"Fixes #N\" or the UI link feature. This is the most reliable signal.\n\n```bash\n# Query issue timeline for cross-referenced or connected PRs\nPR_NUMBER=$(gh api \"/repos/$REPO/issues/$TASK_ISSUE/timeline\" \\\n  --jq '.[] | select(.event == \"cross-referenced\") | select(.source.issue.pull_request != null) | select(.source.issue.state == \"open\") | .source.issue.number' | head -1)\n```\n\n#### Strategy B: Search PR bodies for \"Fixes #N\" or \"#N\"\n\nCopilot PRs typically include \"Fixes #1876\" in the body even when the title is descriptive.\n\n```bash\n# Search open PR bodies for the issue number\nPR_NUMBER=$(gh pr list -R $REPO --state open --json number,body \\\n  --jq \".[] | select(.body | test(\\\"#$TASK_ISSUE\\\")) | .number\" | head -1)\n```\n\n#### Strategy C: Match title or branch name (original approach)\n\n```bash\nPR_NUMBER=$(gh pr list -R $REPO --state open --json number,title,headRefName \\\n  --jq \".[] | select((.title | test(\\\"$TASK_ISSUE\\\"; \\\"i\\\")) or (.headRefName | test(\\\"$TASK_ISSUE\\\"))) | .number\" | head -1)\n```\n\n#### Polling loop\n\nTry all three strategies each iteration. Poll every 30 seconds for up to 15 minutes (Copilot coding agent can take 5-12 minutes to produce a PR).\n\n```bash\nTIMEOUT=900\nINTERVAL=30\nELAPSED=0\n\nwhile [ $ELAPSED -lt $TIMEOUT ]; do\n  # Strategy A: issue timeline\n  PR_NUMBER=$(gh api \"/repos/$REPO/issues/$TASK_ISSUE/timeline\" \\\n    --jq '.[] | select(.event == \"cross-referenced\") | select(.source.issue.pull_request != null) | select(.source.issue.state == \"open\") | .source.issue.number' 2>/dev/null | head -1)\n\n  # Strategy B: PR body search\n  if [ -z \"$PR_NUMBER\" ]; then\n    PR_NUMBER=$(gh pr list -R $REPO --state open --json number,body \\\n      --jq \".[] | select(.body | test(\\\"#$TASK_ISSUE\\\")) | .number\" | head -1)\n  fi\n\n  # Strategy C: title/branch match\n  if [ -z \"$PR_NUMBER\" ]; then\n    PR_NUMBER=$(gh pr list -R $REPO --state open --json number,title,headRefName \\\n      --jq \".[] | select((.title | test(\\\"$TASK_ISSUE\\\"; \\\"i\\\")) or (.headRefName | test(\\\"$TASK_ISSUE\\\"))) | .number\" | head -1)\n  fi\n\n  if [ -n \"$PR_NUMBER\" ]; then\n    break\n  fi\n\n  sleep $INTERVAL\n  ELAPSED=$((ELAPSED + INTERVAL))\ndone\n```\n\nIf no PR is found after timeout, report failure and stop.\n\nOnce the PR is found, verify the base branch as a sanity check (the `agent_assignment.base_branch` API call in Step 1 guarantees this, but confirm):\n\n```bash\n# Sanity-check: confirm PR targets the correct base branch\nACTUAL_BASE=$(gh pr view $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --json baseRefName --jq '.baseRefName')\nif [ \"$ACTUAL_BASE\" != \"$BASE_BRANCH\" ]; then\n  echo \"ERROR: PR #$PR_NUMBER targets '$ACTUAL_BASE' instead of '$BASE_BRANCH'.\"\n  echo \"This should not happen when Step 1 used the agent_assignment.base_branch API.\"\n  echo \"Manual intervention required — stop here.\"\n  exit 1\nfi\necho \"Base branch confirmed: $ACTUAL_BASE\"\n```\n\n### Step 3: Wait for initial commits and workflow trigger\n\nAfter the PR is created, Copilot pushes commits which trigger workflow runs. These runs require approval because every Copilot push triggers the \"Approve workflows to run\" gate.\n\nYou may be coming to this PR after all the runs have been manually approved. In that case, you need to wait for the runs to complete, then, skip to step 6. Here is how you wait for the runs to complete.\n\n```bash\ngh pr checks $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --watch\n```\n\nOtherwise, wait for runs to appear in `action_required` status:\n\n```bash\n# Wait for workflow runs needing approval\ngh run list -R $REPO --branch \"$JTBDTASK_BRANCH\" --status action_required \\\n  --json databaseId,name,status --jq '.[].databaseId'\n```\n\n### Steps 4–5: Approve pending workflow runs and wait for completion\n\nInvoke the **`shepherd-task-approve-workflows-and-wait-for-completion`** skill (`skills/shepherd-task-approve-workflows-and-wait-for-completion/SKILL.md`) with:\n\n- `REPO` = `$REPO`\n- `JTBDTASK_BRANCH` = the PR's topic branch\n- `PR_NUMBER` = `$PR_NUMBER`\n\nThis sub-skill approves all `action_required` runs via `gh run rerun` and waits for completion via `gh pr checks --watch`.\n\n### Step 6: Evaluate workflow results\n\n**Note:** Ignore failures from the \"Block remove-before-merge paths\" / \"No remove-before-merge directories\" workflow. This failure is expected on feature branches and is not a real problem.\n\n```bash\n# Get check results, excluding the expected \"Block remove-before-merge paths\" failure\nRESULTS=$(gh pr checks $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --json name,state,bucket \\\n  --jq '.[] | select(.bucket == \"fail\") | select(.name != \"No remove-before-merge directories\")')\n```\n\nIf there are real failures (after excluding the expected one), proceed to Step 7. If all pass, proceed to Step 8.\n\n### Step 7: Request changes from Copilot (iteration loop)\n\n**Max iterations: 20**\n\nWhen CI fails or review agents flag problems:\n\n#### 7.1: Gather failure details\n\n```bash\n# Get failed run IDs\nFAILED_RUNS=$(gh run list -R $REPO --branch \"$JTBDTASK_BRANCH\" \\\n  --status completed --json databaseId,conclusion,name \\\n  --jq '.[] | select(.conclusion == \"failure\") | .databaseId')\n\n# Get logs for failed runs (only failed steps)\nfor RUN_ID in $FAILED_RUNS; do\n  gh run view $RUN_ID -R $REPO --log-failed\ndone\n```\n\n#### 7.2: Gather review agent comments\n\n```bash\n# Get review comments on the PR\ngh api \"/repos/$REPO/pulls/$PR_NUMBER/comments\" \\\n  --jq '.[] | select(.user.type == \"Bot\") | {user: .user.login, body: .body}'\n\n# Also get issue-level comments (review agents sometimes post there)\ngh pr view $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --comments --json comments \\\n  --jq '.comments[] | select(.author.login | test(\"bot|copilot|agent\"; \"i\")) | {author: .author.login, body: .body}'\n```\n\n#### 7.3: Compose and submit a \"Request changes\" review\n\nAnalyze the failures and compose a hybrid message: relevant log excerpts plus a short targeted instruction for Copilot.\n\n```bash\n# Submit review requesting changes, @mentioning Copilot\ngh pr review $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --request-changes --body \"$REVIEW_BODY\"\n```\n\nThe `$REVIEW_BODY` should follow this format:\n\n```\n@copilot Please fix the following issues:\n\n## CI Failure: [workflow name]\n\n<relevant log excerpt, trimmed to the essential error>\n\n**Fix:** [Short, specific instruction on what to change]\n\n## Review Comment from [bot name]\n\n> [quoted comment]\n\n**Fix:** [Short, specific instruction on what to change]\n```\n\n#### 7.4: Wait for Copilot to push fixes\n\nAfter submitting the review, wait for new commits on the branch:\n\n```bash\n# Get c

If you launch a long-running polling command with a short `initial_wait` and then say \"I'll check back when it completes,\" the runtime will kill the session before the command finishes.\n\n**Rules for all polling and waiting steps:**\n\n1. ✅✅✅ **ALWAYS use `initial_wait` ≥ 600 seconds** (10 minutes) on any polling/waiting command. This keeps the agent blocked on the tool call rather than going idle. ✅✅✅\n2. ❌❌❌ **NEVER background a polling command and then end your turn with no tool calls.** If a command exceeds `initial_wait`, immediately issue another tool call (e.g., `read_powershell`) to stay active. ❌❌❌\n3. ❌❌❌ **NEVER say \"I'll check back when it completes\" or \"Waiting for notification.\"** These phrases mean you are going idle, which KILLS THE SESSION. ❌❌❌\n4. ✅✅✅ **ALWAYS prefer a single blocking poll** over launching a background command and waiting for a notification. ✅✅✅\n\n---\n\n## Procedure\n\n### Step 1: Assign the task to @Copilot\n\nUse the GitHub Issues REST API with the `agent_assignment.base_branch` parameter. That command uses the plain assignees endpoint which has no `base_branch` parameter; CCA will default to `main`.\n\n```bash\ngh api \\\n  --method POST \\\n  -H \"Accept: application/vnd.github+json\" \\\n  -H \"X-GitHub-Api-Version: 2022-11-28\" \\\n  /repos/$REPO/issues/$TASK_ISSUE/assignees \\\n  --input - <<< \"{\n    \\\"assignees\\\": [\\\"copilot-swe-agent[bot]\\\"],\n    \\\"agent_assignment\\\": {\n      \\\"target_repo\\\": \\\"$REPO\\\",\n      \\\"base_branch\\\": \\\"$BASE_BRANCH\\\"\n    }\n  }\"\n```\n\n> **PowerShell equivalent** (when running on Windows):\n> ```powershell\n> $body = @{\n>     assignees        = @(\"copilot-swe-agent[bot]\")\n>     agent_assignment = @{\n>         target_repo = $REPO\n>         base_branch = $BASE_BRANCH\n>     }\n> } | ConvertTo-Json -Depth 3\n> gh api `\n>   --method POST `\n>   -H \"Accept: application/vnd.github+json\" `\n>   -H \"X-GitHub-Api-Version: 2022-11-28\" `\n>   /repos/$REPO/issues/$TASK_ISSUE/assignees `\n>   --input - <<< $body\n> ```\n\nThis triggers Copilot to:\n1. Create a topic branch from `$BASE_BRANCH`.\n2. Open a draft PR targeting `$BASE_BRANCH`.\n3. Push initial commits.\n\n### Step 2: Find the corresponding PR\n\nUse **all three** of the following strategies (in order) each polling iteration. Copilot often creates PRs whose title or branch name does NOT contain the issue number — it may use a descriptive name instead. Therefore, relying on title/branch regex alone is insufficient.\n\n#### Strategy A: Query the issue timeline for linked PRs\n\nThe GitHub timeline API shows PRs linked via \"Fixes #N\" or the UI link feature. This is the most reliable signal.\n\n```bash\n# Query issue timeline for cross-referenced or connected PRs\nPR_NUMBER=$(gh api \"/repos/$REPO/issues/$TASK_ISSUE/timeline\" \\\n  --jq '.[] | select(.event == \"cross-referenced\") | select(.source.issue.pull_request != null) | select(.source.issue.state == \"open\") | .source.issue.number' | head -1)\n```\n\n#### Strategy B: Search PR bodies for \"Fixes #N\" or \"#N\"\n\nCopilot PRs typically include \"Fixes #1876\" in the body even when the title is descriptive.\n\n```bash\n# Search open PR bodies for the issue number\nPR_NUMBER=$(gh pr list -R $REPO --state open --json number,body \\\n  --jq \".[] | select(.body | test(\\\"#$TASK_ISSUE\\\")) | .number\" | head -1)\n```\n\n#### Strategy C: Match title or branch name (original approach)\n\n```bash\nPR_NUMBER=$(gh pr list -R $REPO --state open --json number,title,headRefName \\\n  --jq \".[] | select((.title | test(\\\"$TASK_ISSUE\\\"; \\\"i\\\")) or (.headRefName | test(\\\"$TASK_ISSUE\\\"))) | .number\" | head -1)\n```\n\n#### Polling loop\n\nTry all three strategies each iteration. Poll every 30 seconds for up to 15 minutes (Copilot coding agent can take 5-12 minutes to produce a PR).\n\n```bash\nTIMEOUT=900\nINTERVAL=30\nELAPSED=0\n\nwhile [ $ELAPSED -lt $TIMEOUT ]; do\n  # Strategy A: issue timeline\n  PR_NUMBER=$(gh api \"/repos/$REPO/issues/$TASK_ISSUE/timeline\" \\\n    --jq '.[] | select(.event == \"cross-referenced\") | select(.source.issue.pull_request != null) | select(.source.issue.state == \"open\") | .source.issue.number' 2>/dev/null | head -1)\n\n  # Strategy B: PR body search\n  if [ -z \"$PR_NUMBER\" ]; then\n    PR_NUMBER=$(gh pr list -R $REPO --state open --json number,body \\\n      --jq \".[] | select(.body | test(\\\"#$TASK_ISSUE\\\")) | .number\" | head -1)\n  fi\n\n  # Strategy C: title/branch match\n  if [ -z \"$PR_NUMBER\" ]; then\n    PR_NUMBER=$(gh pr list -R $REPO --state open --json number,title,headRefName \\\n      --jq \".[] | select((.title | test(\\\"$TASK_ISSUE\\\"; \\\"i\\\")) or (.headRefName | test(\\\"$TASK_ISSUE\\\"))) | .number\" | head -1)\n  fi\n\n  if [ -n \"$PR_NUMBER\" ]; then\n    break\n  fi\n\n  sleep $INTERVAL\n  ELAPSED=$((ELAPSED + INTERVAL))\ndone\n```\n\nIf no PR is found after timeout, report failure and stop.\n\nOnce the PR is found, verify the base branch as a sanity check (the `agent_assignment.base_branch` API call in Step 1 guarantees this, but confirm):\n\n```bash\n# Sanity-check: confirm PR targets the correct base branch\nACTUAL_BASE=$(gh pr view $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --json baseRefName --jq '.baseRefName')\nif [ \"$ACTUAL_BASE\" != \"$BASE_BRANCH\" ]; then\n  echo \"ERROR: PR #$PR_NUMBER targets '$ACTUAL_BASE' instead of '$BASE_BRANCH'.\"\n  echo \"This should not happen when Step 1 used the agent_assignment.base_branch API.\"\n  echo \"Manual intervention required — stop here.\"\n  exit 1\nfi\necho \"Base branch confirmed: $ACTUAL_BASE\"\n```\n\n### Step 3: Wait for initial commits and workflow trigger\n\nAfter the PR is created, Copilot pushes commits which trigger workflow runs. These runs require approval because every Copilot push triggers the \"Approve workflows to run\" gate.\n\nYou may be coming to this PR after all the runs have been manually approved. In that case, you need to wait for the runs to complete, then, skip to step 6. Here is how you wait for the runs to complete.\n\n```bash\ngh pr checks $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --watch\n```\n\nOtherwise, wait for runs to appear in `action_required` status:\n\n```bash\n# Wait for workflow runs needing approval\ngh run list -R $REPO --branch \"$JTBDTASK_BRANCH\" --status action_required \\\n  --json databaseId,name,status --jq '.[].databaseId'\n```\n\n### Steps 4–5: Approve pending workflow runs and wait for completion\n\nInvoke the **`shepherd-task-approve-workflows-and-wait-for-completion`** skill (`skills/shepherd-task-approve-workflows-and-wait-for-completion/SKILL.md`) with:\n\n- `REPO` = `$REPO`\n- `JTBDTASK_BRANCH` = the PR's topic branch\n- `PR_NUMBER` = `$PR_NUMBER`\n\nThis sub-skill approves all `action_required` runs via `gh run rerun` and waits for completion via `gh pr checks --watch`.\n\n### Step 6: Evaluate workflow results\n\n**Note:** Ignore failures from the \"Block remove-before-merge paths\" / \"No remove-before-merge directories\" workflow. This failure is expected on feature branches and is not a real problem.\n\n```bash\n# Get check results, excluding the expected \"Block remove-before-merge paths\" failure\nRESULTS=$(gh pr checks $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --json name,state,bucket \\\n  --jq '.[] | select(.bucket == \"fail\") | select(.name != \"No remove-before-merge directories\")')\n```\n\nIf there are real failures (after excluding the expected one), proceed to Step 7. If all pass, proceed to Step 8.\n\n### Step 7: Request changes from Copilot (iteration loop)\n\n**Max iterations: 20**\n\nWhen CI fails or review agents flag problems:\n\n#### 7.1: Gather failure details\n\n```bash\n# Get failed run IDs\nFAILED_RUNS=$(gh run list -R $REPO --branch \"$JTBDTASK_BRANCH\" \\\n  --status completed --json databaseId,conclusion,name \\\n  --jq '.[] | select(.conclusion == \"failure\") | .databaseId')\n\n# Get logs for failed runs (only failed steps)\nfor RUN_ID in $FAILED_RUNS; do\n  gh run view $RUN_ID -R $REPO --log-failed\ndone\n```\n\n#### 7.2: Gather review agent comments\n\n```bash\n# Get review comments on the PR\ngh api \"/repos/$REPO/pulls/$PR_NUMBER/comments\" \\\n  --jq '.[] | select(.user.type == \"Bot\") | {user: .user.login, body: .body}'\n\n# Also get issue-level comments (review agents sometimes post there)\ngh pr view $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --comments --json comments \\\n  --jq '.comments[] | select(.author.login | test(\"bot|copilot|agent\"; \"i\")) | {author: .author.login, body: .body}'\n```\n\n#### 7.3: Compose and submit a \"Request changes\" review\n\nAnalyze the failures and compose a hybrid message: relevant log excerpts plus a short targeted instruction for Copilot.\n\n```bash\n# Submit review requesting changes, @mentioning Copilot\ngh pr review $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --request-changes --body \"$REVIEW_BODY\"\n```\n\nThe `$REVIEW_BODY` should follow this format:\n\n```\n@copilot Please fix the following issues:\n\n## CI Failure: [workflow name]\n\n<relevant log excerpt, trimmed to the essential error>\n\n**Fix:** [Short, specific instruction on what to change]\n\n## Review Comment from [bot name]\n\n> [quoted comment]\n\n**Fix:** [Short, specific instruction on what to change]\n```\n\n#### 7.4: Wait for Copilot to push fixes\n\nAfter submitting the review, wait for new commits on the branch:\n\n```bash\n# Get current HEAD SHA\nCURRENT_SHA=$(gh pr view $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --json headRefOid --jq '.headRefOid')\n\n# Poll for new commits (up to 10 minutes)\nTIMEOUT=600\nINTERVAL=30\nELAPSED=0\n\nwhile [ $ELAPSED -lt $TIMEOUT ]; do\n  NEW_SHA=$(gh pr view $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --json headRefOid --jq '.headRefOid')\n  if [ \"$NEW_SHA\" != \"$CURRENT_SHA\" ]; then\n    break\n  fi\n  sleep $INTERVAL\n  ELAPSED=$((ELAPSED + INTERVAL))\ndone\n```\n\n#### 7.5: Loop back\n\nReturn to **Step 4** (approve workflows) and repeat. Track iteration count. If 20 iterations are ex

{
  "description": "Summarize shepherd-task log files",
  "command": "$base='C:\\Users\\edburns\\workareas\\BRK206-02\\28-python-agent-demo-remove-before-merge';\n$dirs=@('shepherd-tasks-20260717-1936','shepherd-tasks-20260717-2022','shepherd-tasks-20260718-1648','shepherd-tasks-20260718-1827');\n$all=@();\nforeach($d in $dirs){\n  $path=Join-Path $base $d;\n  Get-ChildItem -Path $path -File | ForEach-Object {\n    $f=$_;\n    if($f.Extension -eq '.json'){\n      $lines=Get-Content -Path $f.FullName;\n      $objs=@();\n      foreach($line in $lines){ if($line.Trim()){ try{$objs += ($line | ConvertFrom-Json)}catch{} } }\n      $ts=$objs | Where-Object { $_.timestamp } | Select-Object -ExpandProperty timestamp;\n      $firstTs=if($ts){ ($ts | Sort-Object | Select-Object -First 1) } else { '' };\n      $lastTs=if($ts){ ($ts | Sort-Object | Select-Object -Last 1) } else { '' };\n      $idleCount=($objs | Where-Object { $_.type -eq 'assistant.idle' }).Count;\n      $toolReqs=($objs | Where-Object { $_.type -eq 'assistant.message' } | ForEach-Object { if($_.data.toolRequests){ $_.data.toolRequests.Count } else {0} } | Measure-Object -Sum).Sum;\n      $toolExec=($objs | Where-Object { $_.type -eq 'tool.execution_complete' });\n      $toolFail=($toolExec | Where-Object { $_.data.success -eq $false }).Count;\n      $toolOk=($toolExec | Where-Object { $_.data.success -eq $true }).Count;\n      $outTokens=($objs | Where-Object { $_.type -eq 'assistant.message' } | ForEach-Object { if($_.data.outputTokens){ [int]$_.data.outputTokens } else {0} } | Measure-Object -Sum).Sum;\n      $inTokens=($objs | Where-Object { $_.type -eq 'assistant.message' } | ForEach-Object { if($_.data.inputTokens){ [int]$_.data.inputTokens } else {0} } | Measure-Object -Sum).Sum;\n      $all += [pscustomobject]@{Dir=$d;File=$f.Name;Kind='json';First=$firstTs;Last=$lastTs;Idle=$idleCount;ToolRequests=$toolReqs;ToolExecOk=$toolOk;ToolExecFail=$toolFail;InputTokens=$inTokens;OutputTokens=$outTokens;SizeKB=[math]::Round($f.Length/1kb,1)};\n    } elseif($f.Extension -eq '.md'){\n      $text=Get-Content -Path $f.FullName -Raw;\n      $started=[regex]::Match($text,'\\*\\*Started:\\*\\*\\s+([^\\r\\n]+)').Groups[1].Value;\n      $duration=[regex]::Match($text,'\\*\\*Duration:\\*\\*\\s+([^\\r\\n]+)').Groups[1].Value;\n      $exported=[regex]::Match($text,'\\*\\*Exported:\\*\\*\\s+([^\\r\\n]+)').Groups[1].Value;\n      $timeouts=([regex]::Matches($text,'still running after 120 seconds')).Count;\n      $waiting=([regex]::Matches($text,'I.ll check back when')).Count;\n      $all += [pscustomobject]@{Dir=$d;File=$f.Name;Kind='md';Started=$started;Duration=$duration;Exported=$exported;Timeout120=$timeouts;IdlePhrase=$waiting;SizeKB=[math]::Round($f.Length/1kb,1)};\n    }\n  }\n}\n'=== FILE SUMMARY ===';\n$all | Sort-Object Dir,File | Format-Table -AutoSize | Out-String -Width 400;\n'=== JSON ROLLUP BY DIR ===';\n$all | Where-Object Kind -eq 'json' | Group-Object Dir | ForEach-Object {\n  $g=$_.Group;\n  [pscustomobject]@{Dir=$_.Name;JsonFiles=$g.Count;IdleEvents=($g|Measure-Object Idle -Sum).Sum;ToolReq=($g|Measure-Object ToolRequests -Sum).Sum;ToolFail=($g|Measure-Object ToolExecFail -Sum).Sum;OutputTokens=($g|Measure-Object OutputTokens -Sum).Sum;First=($g.First|Sort-Object|Select-Object -First 1);Last=($g.Last|Sort-Object|Select-Object -Last 1)}\n} | Sort-Object Dir | Format-Table -AutoSize | Out-String -Width 400;\n'=== MD TIMEOUT/IDLE-PHRASE FLAGS ===';\n$all | Where-Object Kind -eq 'md' | Where-Object { $_.Timeout120 -gt 0 -or $_.IdlePhrase -gt 0 } | Sort-Object Dir,File | Format-Table -AutoSize | Out-String -Width 400;",
  "initial_wait": 120

86. 
87. ### 19:59 Prompt
88. 
89. ### Technology stack
90. 
91. Another agent recommended the following technology stack for a green field python CRUD+AI app. I'm ignorant of the Python world. Does this seem reasonably contemporary for 2026-07?
92. 
93. | Concern | Technology |
94. |---------|-----------|
95. | Runtime | CPython 3.12+ (virtualenv project) |
96. | Backend web framework | FastAPI (ASGI, asyncio-native) |
97. | ASGI server | Uvicorn |
98. | UI framework | Server-rendered Jinja2 + HTMX + Alpine.js + Tailwind CSS |
99. | Real-time updates | FastAPI WebSocket endpoint broadcasting pipeline state changes |
100. | Animation model | CSS transitions/keyframes for box-to-box movement + yellow pulsing in-progress indicator |
101. | AI orchestration | GitHub Copilot SDK for Python (latest stable at implementation time) |
102. | Database | SQLite (in-memory for demo mode) via SQLModel |
103. | Build / dependency management | `pyproject.toml` + editable install (`pip install -e .[dev]`), with `uv` as optional fast path |
104. | Tooling | `pytest`, `pytest-asyncio`, `ruff`, `pyright` |
105. 
106. ### 20:03 Response
107. 
108. This is a solid, well-chosen stack overall. A few comments on each layer:
109. 
110. **Clearly good picks:**
111. - **FastAPI + Uvicorn** remains the default choice for new async Python APIs. Nothing has displaced it.
112. - **Jinja2 + HTMX + Alpine.js + Tailwind** is the "modern hypermedia" stack that's been gaining momentum as a counterpoint to full SPA frameworks. It's a natural fit for a server-rendered CRUD app where you want interactivity without shipping a JS build pipeline.
113. - **SQLModel** is from the same author as FastAPI (Sebastián Ramírez), so the Pydantic model integration is seamless — one model class serves as your DB schema, API schema, and validation layer.
114. - **ruff + pyright** have essentially won. Ruff replaced flake8, black, and isort in one tool; pyright is the standard type checker.
115. - **`uv`** from Astral (same team as ruff) is the ascendant package/project manager — calling it "optional fast path" is almost underselling it at this point; many greenfield projects use it as the primary tool.
116. - **CSS keyframes for animation** — you already know this pattern from the PrimeFaces port. Same browser-native approach, just triggered differently.
117. 
118. **Minor version note:**
119. - **CPython 3.12+** is a safe floor, but Python 3.13 (Oct 2024) and 3.14 (Oct 2025) are both out by now. A greenfield project could comfortably target **3.13+** to pick up the free-threading groundwork and improved error messages, unless a dependency pins you lower.
120. 
121. **The one I'd scrutinize:**
122. - **"GitHub Copilot SDK for Python"** is the entry I'd push back on. Copilot is primarily a code-completion tool integrated into IDEs, not an AI orchestration library you'd embed in a runtime application to, say, call an LLM as part of a pipeline. If the goal is to make LLM calls from your app (generate text, classify, summarize, etc.), the typical choices would be calling a provider SDK directly (Anthropic SDK, OpenAI SDK) or using an orchestration layer if you need chaining, tool use, or agent loops. I'd ask the recommending agent to clarify what it actually meant — it may have hallucinated a library that doesn't exist in the form described, which is a common failure mode for AI-generated stack recommendations.
123. 
124. Everything else looks like a stack a well-informed Python developer would pick today.
125. 
126.
```

</details>

80. 
81. Here's the timeline:
82. 
83. ```
84. ┌──────────┬──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
85. │ Time     │ Event                                                    │
86. ├──────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
87. │ 00:23:05 │ Session started                                          │
88. ├──────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
89. │ 00:23:30 │ Requested Copilot review ✅                              │

91. │ 00:23:42 │ Started polling loop                                     │
92. ├──────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
93. │ 00:25:17 │ Poll at 90s — initial_wait: 120 hasn't expired yet       │
94. ├──────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
95. │ 00:25:41 │ Turn 3 ends (initial_wait expired, command backgrounded) │
96. ├──────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
97. │ 00:25:45 │ assistant.idle — agent has no more work, goes idle       │
98. ├──────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
99. │ 00:26:51 │ Poll finds review at 180s — but session already ended    │
100. ├──────────┼──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤
101. │ 00:26:51 │ result: null — session terminated                        │
102. └──────────┴──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
103. ```
104. 
105. Root cause: The `copilot --yolo` session has an idle timeout. Once the polling command exceeded `initial_wait: 120s` and was backgrounded, the agent said "I'll check back when the polling completes" and went idle. The `assistant.idle` event fired at 00:25:45, and ~66 seconds later the session was killed — even though the background command was still running and actually found the review.
106. 
107. This is an externally imposed idle timeout, not a skill bug. The `--yolo` mode appears to terminate the session shortly after the agent goes idle (no pending tool calls from the agent's perspective). The background shell command was still running, but the runtime treats the agent as "done" once it's idle.
108. 
109. Contrast with BRK206-01: In that run, sessions lasted 22 min to 10+ hours. Either the idle timeout didn't exist in that CLI version, or the agent structured its polling differently (not backgrounding the command).
110. 
111. Fix options:
112. 
113. 1. Have the agent use a shorter `initial_wait` that doesn't exceed the idle timeout — but then it needs to actively loop itself rather than relying on background commands
114. 2. The skill should instruct the agent to never go idle while waiting — instead of backgrounding the poll, it should block on it with a long `initial_wait` (e.g., 600s)
115. 
116. ### 16:42 Prompt

1985. 
1986. When I look at it, I observe that there is a **Request** button next to **Copilot** in the **Reviewers** area. 
1987. 
1988. Does this mean that copilot review is not automatically requested when the PR is taken out of draft state?
1989. 
1990. ### 20:15 Response
1991. 
1992. !Yes, that's correct. Copilot code review is not automatically requested when a PR is taken out of draft.
1993. 
1994. The `gh pr view` confirms it: `reviewRequests` only shows `edburns` — Copilot is not in the list, and `reviews` is empty.
1995. 
1996. The phase 2 skill was polling forever for a review that was never going to arrive, because it assumed marking the PR as ready would trigger Copilot review automatically.
1997. 
1998. The fix is that the skill procedure needs an explicit step after `gh pr ready`:
1999. 
2000. gh pr edit $PR_NUMBER -R $REPO --add-reviewer "copilot-pull-request-reviewer"
2001. 
2002. This is actually already in the skill at Step 12 (re-request review after fixing comments), but it's missing from Step 1 (the initial ready-for-review flow). The skill just does `gh pr ready` and immediately starts polling — but nobody ever requested Copilot as a reviewer.
2003. 
2004. Want me to fix the skill to add the explicit review request after Step 1?
2005. 
2006. ### 20:16 Prompt
2007. 
2008. What skill would you be touching?
2009. 
2010. ### 20:16 Response
2011. 
2012. The skill that needs fixing is `shepherd-task-from-ready-to-merged-to-base`, located at:
2013. 
2014. C:\Users\edburns\.copilot\skills\shepherd-task-from-ready-to-merged-to-base\SKILL.md
2015. 
2016. Specifically, after Step 1 (`gh pr ready`), it should add an explicit `gh pr edit --add-reviewer "copilot-pull-request-reviewer"` before entering the Step 2 polling loop.
2017. 
2018. ### 20:16 Prompt
2019. 
2020. Yes. Please fix that skill.
2021. 
2022. ### 20:17 Response
2023. 
2024. Done. The fix:
2025. 
2026. 1. Added `gh pr edit --add-reviewer "copilot-pull-request-reviewer"` after `gh pr ready`
2027. 2. Removed the incorrect comment that marking as ready "triggers" Copilot review
2028. 3. Added a note clarifying the explicit request is required
2029. 
2030. ### 20:17 Prompt
2031. 
2032. Now, I recall from a previous run that the Phase 1 skill `shepherd-task-from-assignment-to-ready` was made idempotent so that I could invoke 
2033. 
2034. ```
2035. . .\plugins\shepherd-task\scripts\shepherd-task-given-list.ps1 "41,33,34,35,36,37,38,39" edburns/28-python-agent-demo edburns/Build26-BRK206-your-agent-anywhere-multiclient-multidevice-with-github-copilot-sdk
2036. ```
2037. 
2038. and it would start with issue 41, see that Phase 1 was already completed, and then proceed to Phase 2 `shepherd-task-from-ready-to-merged-to-base/`. Please confirm this. Ask me if you can't find any files you need to find.
2039. 
2040. ### 20:20 Response
2041. 
2042. Confirmed. The idempotency is in `shepherd-task.ps1` lines 116–146:
2043. 
2044. - Line 116: `Find-LinkedPR` checks if a PR already exists for issue #41
2045. - Line 117–118: If PR #42 is found, it prints "PR #42 already exists — skipping Phase 1"
2046. - Lines 149–168: It still verifies base branch, CI, and reviews before proceeding to Phase 2
2047. 
2048. So re-running with `"41,33,34,35,36,37,38,39"` will:
2049. 
2050. 1. Issue #41: Find PR #42, skip Phase 1, verify state, then run Phase 2 (which will now correctly request Copilot review thanks to our fix)
2051. 2. Issues #33–39: Run normally from Phase 1
2052. 
2053. One caveat: `shepherd-task-given-list.ps1` line 44–47 stops on first failure (`exit $LASTEXITCODE`). So if #41's Phase 2 fails again, it won't attempt #33–39.
2054. 
2055.

54. ## Section 1: Executive Summary
55. 
56. Epic [#2](https://github.com/edburns/Build26-BRK206-your-agent-anywhere-multiclient-multidevice-with-github-copilot-sdk/issues/2) tasked a three-agent pipeline with implementing a complete Java EE 11 + OpenLiberty port of the BRK206 real-estate demo across 9 discrete sub-issues (sections 3.1–3.9 of the implementation plan). Two additional sub-issues were aborted before completion and excluded from this analysis.
57.

60. | Sub-issues attempted | 11 |
61. | Sub-issues completed (merged) | 9 |

75. ---
76. 
77. ## Section 2: System Architecture
78. 
79. The pipeline consisted of three collaborating agents:
80. 
81. ### 2.1 Copilot Coding Agent (CCA)
82. 
83. The CCA performed the initial implementation of each issue. It ran on GitHub's infrastructure, triggered by assigning the issue to Copilot. For 8 of 9 tasks, the `shepherd-task-to-ready` skill (phase 1) monitored the CCA run, polled for PR creation and CI completion, and approved any pending workflow runs. Issue [#13](https://github.com/edburns/Build26-BRK206-your-agent-anywhere-multiclient-multidevice-with-github-copilot-sdk/issues/13)'s CCA had already completed before the first shepherd batch started.
84. 
85. The CCA produced draft PRs targeting the `edburns/2-build-out-demo` base branch. Initial implementations ranged from 1 commit (issue [#11](https://github.com/edburns/Build26-BRK206-your-agent-anywhere-multiclient-multidevice-with-github-copilot-sdk/issues/11)) to 7 commits (issue [#20](https://github.com/edburns/Build26-BRK206-your-agent-anywhere-multiclient-multidevice-with-github-copilot-sdk/issues/20)) before any CCRA involvement.
86. 
87. ### 2.2 Copilot Code Review Agent (CCRA)
88. 
89. The CCRA (`copilot-pull-request-reviewer[bot]`) reviewed each PR once it was marked "Ready for Review." It posted inline comments identifying bugs, missing requirements, style violations, and constraint violations. The CCRA ran on GitHub's infrastructure asynchronously, typically completing a review within 5–15 minutes of being requested.
90. 
91. ### 2.3 Local Copilot CLI (Shepherd)
92. 
93. The local CLI (`copilot --yolo`) ran the `shepherd-task-from-ready-to-merged-to-base` skill (phase 2). For each CCRA review batch, it:
94. 
95. 1. Fetched and read all open review comments
96. 2. Applied each fix locally (via `edit`, `create`, or `powershell` tool calls in a worktree)
97. 3. Made a single commit per batch and pushed to the head branch
98. 4. Re-requested a CCRA review
99. 5. Repeated until no comments remained or 8 rounds were reached
100. 6. Merged the PR via `gh pr merge`
101. 
102. The local CLI ran in `--yolo` mode, autonomously approving all tool permission requests. Each phase-2 session was a single long-lived `copilot` process that polled GitHub for CCRA completion between rounds.
103. 
104. ---

  "initial_wait": 120
}

}

### `view`

**view the file at C:\Users\edburns\workareas\BRK206-02\28-python-agent-demo-remove-before-merge\shepherd-tasks-20260718-1827\20260718-1855-copilot-cli-otel-not-working.md.**

C:\Users\edburns\workareas\BRK206-02\28-python-agent-demo-remove-before-merge\shepherd-tasks-20260718-1827\20260718-1855-copilot-cli-otel-not-working.md

<details>
<summary>101 lines</summary>

````
1. # Bug: OTEL file exporter never flushes when `copilot` is invoked via piped stdin
2. 
3. ## Summary
4. 
5. When `copilot --yolo` is invoked with a prompt piped to stdin (without `-p`), the OpenTelemetry file exporter is initialized successfully but never flushes spans to disk on shutdown. The OTEL `.jsonl` file is never created. The same configuration works correctly when using `-p` (non-interactive prompt mode).
6. 
7. ## Version
8. 
9. ```
10. copilot 1.0.72-1
11. Node.js v24.16.0
12. Windows 11 (also likely affects Linux/macOS — untested)
13. ```
14. 
15. ## Reproducer
16. 
17. ### ✅ Works: `-p` flag (non-interactive prompt mode)
18. 
19. ```powershell
20. $env:COPILOT_OTEL_FILE_EXPORTER_PATH = "C:\temp\otel-test-works.jsonl"
21. copilot -p "what is 2+2" --yolo --output-format json 2>&1 | Out-Null
22. Remove-Item Env:\COPILOT_OTEL_FILE_EXPORTER_PATH
23. Test-Path "C:\temp\otel-test-works.jsonl"  # True — file created, ~17KB
24. ```
25. 
26. ### ❌ Broken: piped stdin (interactive mode with stdin EOF)
27. 
28. ```powershell
29. $env:COPILOT_OTEL_FILE_EXPORTER_PATH = "C:\temp\otel-test-broken.jsonl"
30. "what is 2+2" | copilot --yolo --output-format json > $null
31. Remove-Item Env:\COPILOT_OTEL_FILE_EXPORTER_PATH
32. Test-Path "C:\temp\otel-test-broken.jsonl"  # False — file never created
33. ```
34. 
35. ### Bash equivalent
36. 
37. ```bash
38. # Works
39. COPILOT_OTEL_FILE_EXPORTER_PATH=/tmp/otel-works.jsonl copilot -p "what is 2+2" --yolo --output-format json > /dev/null 2>&1
40. ls -la /tmp/otel-works.jsonl  # exists
41. 
42. # Broken
43. COPILOT_OTEL_FILE_EXPORTER_PATH=/tmp/otel-broken.jsonl sh -c 'echo "what is 2+2" | copilot --yolo --output-format json > /dev/null'
44. ls -la /tmp/otel-broken.jsonl  # does not exist
45. ```
46. 
47. ## Diagnostic Evidence
48. 
49. ### Process log confirms OTEL is enabled
50. 
51. From `~/.copilot/logs/process-1784413641486-14644.log` (the piped-stdin invocation):
52. 
53. ```
54. 2026-07-18T22:27:22.134Z [INFO] OpenTelemetry enabled: exporter=file, source=github.copilot
55. ```
56. 
57. OTEL initializes correctly. The env var is read and the file exporter is selected.
58. 
59. ### Shutdown sequence has no OTEL flush
60. 
61. The same log's shutdown sequence:
62. 
63. ```
64. 2026-07-18T22:51:40.526Z [DEBUG] [shutdown] Completed dispose: M6 (27ms)
65. 2026-07-18T22:51:40.785Z [DEBUG] [shutdown] Completed dispose: a6 (286ms)
66. 2026-07-18T22:51:40.787Z [DEBUG] [shutdown] Completed dispose: closeSessionStore (2ms)
67. 2026-07-18T22:51:40.788Z [DEBUG] [shutdown] Completed dispose: logger (1ms)
68. 2026-07-18T22:51:40.788Z [DEBUG] [shutdown] Shutdown complete
69. ```
70. 
71. There is **no OTEL exporter dispose/flush step** in the shutdown sequence. The spans collected in memory are never written to disk. No error is logged.
72. 
73. ### Other session artifacts ARE written
74. 
75. The same invocation successfully writes:
76. - `--share` markdown file (144KB) ✅
77. - `--output-format json` stdout capture (2.8MB) ✅
78. - Session store updates ✅
79. 
80. Only the OTEL file exporter output is missing.
81. 
82. ## Impact
83. 
84. This blocks using `COPILOT_OTEL_FILE_EXPORTER_PATH` for offline/CI observability in any pipeline that invokes `copilot` via piped stdin — which is the standard pattern for orchestration scripts like:
85. 
86. ```powershell
87. $prompt | copilot --yolo --output-format json --share $sharePath > $jsonPath
88. ```
89. 
90. This is the invocation pattern used by the shepherd-task orchestration scripts that drive multi-issue agentic workflows (assign → PR → review → merge).
91. 
92. ## Expected Behavior
93. 
94. The OTEL file exporter should flush all buffered spans to the specified file path during the shutdown sequence, regardless of whether the session was started via `-p` or piped stdin.
95. 
96. ## Suggested Investigation
97. 
98. 1. The `-p` code path likely calls an explicit OTEL shutdown/flush. The piped-stdin (interactive mode with EOF) shutdown path likely skips it.
99. 2. Look for the dispose/shutdown handler that calls the Rust OTEL file exporter's flush — it's probably registered in the `-p` path but not in the interactive-mode graceful-exit path.
100. 3. The shutdown dispose chain (`M6` → `a6` → `closeSessionStore` → `logger`) should include an OTEL exporter flush step before `logger` dispose.
101.
````

</details>

Keep explicit reviewer-request step in phase-2 skill as a non-optional invariant.\n+2. Keep idle-prevention directives in all shepherd skills; treat as runtime safety constraints.\n+3. Add explicit exit-code checks around critical branch-target operations (`gh pr edit --base`) in `shepherd-task.ps1`.\n+4. Record one top-level job log for every batch (not only the final successful one) to simplify forensic reconstruction.\n+5. Continue using CCRA round/comment counts as primary quality metric until OTEL flush issue is fixed.\n+\n+### 8.4 Comparison to prior Java run (BRK206-01)\n+\n+The Java post-mortem reported phase-2 sessions spanning 22 minutes to 10+ hours, with PR #43 converging in 7 rounds over 52 minutes. This Python campaign ultimately matched that convergence capability (e.g., #39 with 7 rounds) after runtime/skill hardening, but required additional stabilization due to idle-kill and review-request gaps discovered during early runs.\n*** End Patch\n"

The final batch (`shepherd-tasks-20260718-1827`) completed **6/6 tasks (100%)**, merged **PRs #44-#49**, and ended with `=== All tasks shepherded successfully ===` in `20260718-1826-job-logs.txt`.

45. 
46. CCA generated or updated draft PRs for task issues. In this campaign, it produced PRs #42-#49, with final successful shepherding focused on #44-#49.
47. 
48. ### 2.2 Copilot Code Review Agent (CCRA)
49. 
50. CCRA (`copilot-pull-request-reviewer[bot]`) produced review rounds with "Comments generated" summaries. Final batch behavior ranged from zero-comment clean review (task #37) to long iterative convergence (task #39, 7 rounds).
51. 
52. ### 2.3 Local Copilot CLI (Shepherd)
53. 
54. `copilot --yolo` ran the two shepherd skills and executed the local merge orchestration loop:
55. 
56. 1. Move issue/PR through phase gates.
57. 2. Request and poll CCRA review.
58. 3. Apply/fix/reply/resolve review feedback.
59. 4. Re-request review until clean.
60. 5. Merge PR to `edburns/28-python-agent-demo`.
61.

116. 
117. ### 5.1 Local Copilot CLI (from JSON logs)
118. 
119. | Scope | Output tokens |
120. |-------|---------------|
121. | Final success batch (`20260718-1827`) | 136,022 |
122. | All four referenced run directories combined | 186,132 |
123. 
124. ### 5.2 CCA / CCRA credits
125. 
126. Direct credit/billing totals were not captured in these artifacts. This report therefore uses review rounds/comments and CLI token totals as the measurable proxy.
127. 
128. ### 5.3 OTEL limitation
129. 
130. `20260718-1855-copilot-cli-otel-not-working.md` documents that OTEL file export does not flush when `copilot` is invoked via piped stdin (bug `copilot-agent-runtime#13047`), limiting observability fidelity for this campaign.
131. 
132. ---
133. 
134. ## Section 6: Wall-Clock Timeline
135. 
136. ### 6.1 Batch timeline
137. 
138. | Batch | Window | Summary |
139. |------|--------|---------|
140. | `20260717-1936` | ~19:36-19:59 ET | First failure on issue #41 phase 2 (PR #42 remained open) |
141. | `20260717-2022` | ~20:23-20:26 ET | Retry failed; review arrived but session had gone idle |
142. | `20260718-1648` | ~16:49-18:09 ET | Stabilization run; #41 and #33 merged, #34 prepared |
143. | `20260718-1827` | ~18:27-22:34 ET | Final run; #34-#39 all merged |
144. 
145. ### 6.2 Final successful run (`20260718-1827`)
146. 
147. - Start marker: `phase2-task-20260718-1827-34.*` (18:27 ET).
148. - End marker: `phase2-task-20260718-2155-39.*` with 39m 20s duration (ends ~22:34 ET).
149. - Top-level log confirms terminal success for all six tasks.
150. 
151. ---
152. 
153. ## Section 7: What Failed Before the Final Run
154. 
155. ### 7.1 Missing initial Copilot review request
156. 
157. Earlier phase-2 logic assumed `gh pr ready` implicitly triggered Copilot review. It does not. This caused polling loops to wait on reviews that were never requested.  
158. Fix: explicit `gh pr edit $PR_NUMBER --add-reviewer "copilot-pull-request-reviewer"` in Step 1 of the phase-2 skill.
159. 
160. ### 7.2 Idle-kill session behavior
161. 
162. In failed runs, phase-2 polling exceeded `initial_wait` and then the assistant emitted "I'll check back..." and went idle. Session logs show `assistant.idle` shortly before termination, while poll output continued in the background.
163. 
164. Fixes applied to skills:
165. 
166. 1. Explicit "never go idle while waiting" directive.
167. 2. Long blocking polls (`initial_wait >= 600`) for wait steps.
168. 3. Ban on ending turn while relying on background poll completion.
169. 
170. ### 7.3 Intermediate run evidence (`20260718-1648`)
171. 
172. - Demonstrated the fixes working: issue #41 merged with `Comments generated: 0`; issue #33 converged through 8 rounds to clean review then merged.
173. - Also exposed remaining friction (timeouts in polling strategy, handoff to next batch for issue #34).
174. 
175. ---
176. 
177. ## Section 8: Observations and Recommendations
178. 
179. ### 8.1 What worked well
180. 
181. - The final batch reached **100% merge completion** for all target tasks.
182. - Review-loop convergence was robust even on deep cycles (#39 with 7 rounds).
183. - Idempotent "skip phase 1 if PR already exists" behavior enabled recovery and reruns.
184. 
185. ### 8.2 What did not work well
186. 
187. - Idle/timeout interaction caused repeated early failures before hardening.
188. - Review-detection/polling logic remained noisy and complex, with repeated long polls.
189. - OTEL exporter bug removed expected telemetry for post-run diagnostics.
190. 
191. ### 8.3 Recommendations
192. 
193. 1. Keep explicit reviewer-request step in phase-2 skill as a non-optional invariant.
194. 2. Keep idle-prevention directives in all shepherd skills; treat as runtime safety constraints.
195. 3. Add explicit exit-code checks around critical branch-target operations (`gh pr edit --base`) in `shepherd-task.ps1`.
196. 4. Record one top-level job log for every batch (not only the final successful one) to simplify forensic reconstruction.
197. 5. Continue using CCRA round/comment counts as primary quality metric until OTEL flush issue is fixed.
198. 
199. ### 8.4 Comparison to prior Java run (BRK206-01)
200. 
201. The Java post-mortem reported phase-2 sessions spanning 22 minutes to 10+ hours, with PR #43 converging in 7 rounds over 52 minutes. This Python campaign ultimately matched that convergence capability (e.g., #39 with 7 rounds) after runtime/skill hardening, but required additional stabilization due to idle-kill and review-request gaps discovered during early runs.
